It didn't take long for news to break that Tim Tibesar would no longer be Purdue's defensive coordinator. Just yesterday, we found out that Greg Hudson, the linebackers coach at Florida State, would be taking over as the team's new defensive coordinator under the guidance of coach Darrell Hazle. FSU's affiliate on Scout.com broke the news, citing sources that indicate Hudson has accepted the offer. I'm thrilled with this development, as Florida State's defense was actually effective this season, stifling several strong offenses in games I had a chance to watch closely. In their matchup against Miami, the Hurricanes took an early 10-0 lead, but the Seminoles' defense managed to shut them down for the remainder of the game. Hudson has experience as a defensive coordinator, having held the position at East Carolina from 2005 to 2009. During his tenure, the Pirates went 5-6, 7-6, 8-5, and 9-5, with a stout defense that earned a pair of Conference-USA championships. The 2008 season was particularly notable, as the Pirates started the year with victories over Virginia Tech and West Virginia, only to see Virginia Tech win the ACC and the Orange Bowl that season. Hudson has also coached linebackers at Cincinnati, Minnesota, and Florida State, where he played for two seasons at Notre Dame. This season was a standout one for FSU, as the Seminoles finished 12-2, won the ACC, and won the Orange Bowl with a defense-first approach. The team allowed just 14.7 points per game, and held teams to 10 or fewer points six times in 14 games. Christian Jones is one of the top-rated linebackers in the country, and Hudson's guidance could help fix the team's struggling linebacker unit. Since the departure of Niko Koutouvides and Landon Johnson a decade ago, Purdue has had a revolving door of decent but not great linebackers, resulting in a struggling defensive unit.
In Tokyo, a renowned composer celebrated for his prolific works in video games and figure skating routines was exposed as a hoaxer. Dubbed Japan's modern-day Beethoven due to his deafness, Mamoru Samuragochi, 50, had fabricated his hearing disability and hired a ghostwriter to pen most of his famous compositions since the 1990s. The revelation sparked widespread outrage and remorse across Japan, with many calling for a lawsuit. However, the ghostwriter soon came forward, accusing Samuragochi of faking his deafness to garner public sympathy and create the Beethoven persona. The scandal began on Wednesday when Samuragochi confessed that someone else had written his most iconic pieces, including Symphony No. 1 "Hiroshima," the theme music for Resident Evil and Onimusha, and Sonatina for Violin, which is set to be used by a Japanese Olympic figure skater in the Sochi Olympics.
A group of feminist academics in France have spoken out against plans to make street harassment illegal, arguing that the new laws could unfairly target men with migrant backgrounds. They claim that such laws would "stigmatize" these men, who already face higher rates of police violence and oppression. The academics, who signed a letter opposing the plans, suggest that training perpetrators on the ground could be a more effective solution. They argue that creating a new offence would only serve to further repress and control men from disadvantaged groups. In their letter, published in the newspaper Libération, the academics express concerns that the plans will only target street harassment and fail to address abuse that occurs in other settings, such as at home and in the workplace. They warn that making street harassment a crime could lead to a lack of accountability for abuse committed in more affluent areas, such as high-end districts and corporate offices. The equality minister, Marlène Schiappa, had previously stated that street harassment can take many forms, including unwanted advances in crowded public places. Speaking about the proposed legislation, she said that it would cover situations like the one she described, where a man follows a woman in a crowded train carriage, repeatedly asking for her phone number despite her discomfort. The move follows surveys that have highlighted the prevalence of street harassment in certain parts of France, including a 2015 study that found that 100% of women in migrant-heavy districts had experienced some form of sexual harassment or assault. Some areas of Paris, such as the Chapelle-Pajol district, have become notorious for their high levels of harassment and assault, with women reporting that they can no longer leave their homes without being subjected to verbal abuse by migrants.
Cisco has announced that several of its Adaptive Security Appliance (ASA) products are vulnerable to a remote code execution bug due to a flaw in the fragmentation protocol used by the devices. The issue arises from how the ASA products reassemble Internet Key Exchange (IKE) payloads, specifically because the implementation has a bounds-checking flaw. According to Exodus Intel, the bug allows an attacker to overflow a heap buffer with malicious data, leading to the remote code execution vulnerability. Affected products include the ASA 5500, ASA 5500-X, ASA Services Module for Catalyst 6500 switches and 7600 Series routers, the ASA 1000V Cloud Firewall, the Adaptive Security Virtual Appliance, the Firepower 9300 ASA module, and the ISA 3000. Both IPv4 and IPv6 traffic can be used to trigger the vulnerability. The problem lies in the code, where the fragment length is 16 bits, but the queues are limited to 8 bits, resulting in an overflow during reassembly. This can be exploited by an attacker to force the target system to reload, and ultimately gain control of the device. Cisco has released a patch for affected software versions.
Imagine six friends gathered in a pub. The first friend says, 'My glass is half empty, I think I need another drink.' The second friend responds, 'My glass is half full, I'm good for now.' The third friend notices a long line at the bar and suggests they wait a moment. The fourth friend counters, 'We'll wait anyway, so why not order two rounds and let loose while we're here?' The fifth friend decides to leave, feeling uninterested in arguing or waiting. Meanwhile, the sixth friend takes charge, ordering everyone's drinks while they debate their next move. The moral of the story is that pessimists always crave more, optimists seem overly content, realists can be frustrating, cynics stir up trouble, quitters are inconsequential, and opportunist friends always have a good time. So, the next time you're out with friends, remember to enjoy yourself more and avoid unnecessary arguments – after all, someone else will likely have more fun at your expense if you don't.

As your adult children prepare to move back in, try to pretend you're not home. A recent survey of 9,000 Fidelity Investments employees and Stanford Center on Longevity found that one in nine baby boomer parents have welcomed their adult children back into the fold within the past year. While it's true that these young adults save money on rent and household expenses, their parents are the ones who appear to be struggling: 68% reported feeling more stressed, 53% said they were less happy, and another 53% reported having less free time after their children returned home. Furthermore, over three-quarters of parents reported taking on higher expenses as a result of their children's return. Even those now in their 40s and 50s are considering their parents as a viable option for housing. According to separate data from Trulia, older millennials are 2.7 times more likely to live with their parents than people under 55, while Generation-Xers are 2.2 times as likely to do so, compared to 1999. Katie Taylor, vice president of thought leadership at Fidelity, notes that "no parent wants to say no to a child in need, but it's essential to be realistic about the financial situation." The trend of multigenerational households is on the rise, with 19% of the US population (or nearly 61 million people) living together, up from 17% in 2009 and 12% in 1980, according to the Pew Research Center. However, not all millennials are "lazy" or "entitled." About one in four 25- to 34-year-olds who live at home are doing so due to health reasons or caregiving for family members. Many Americans, including millennials, also expect to financially help their parents in the near future, with over a third planning to do so. Some are even taking steps to help their parents save for retirement.

A collection of previously unpublished photographs from the Second Boer War has been discovered in a house in Derbyshire. The images, which include battle scenes from the conflict, will go up for auction in July. The find is considered a valuable historical treasure, offering a glimpse into the war that sheds new light on the period. The photographs were taken by Robert Oliver, who survived the war and was awarded the Queen's Medal for South Africa for his service. Oliver's images depict the harsh reality and true horror of war, which was not publicly portrayed at the time due to the British Empire's perceived invincibility. The collection includes photographs of war dead lying in fields, the funeral of a British serviceman, and a Boer War dog, all of which provide a poignant insight into the conflict. In addition to the photographs, the collection also contains items such as hats, gloves, medals, and a South African feathered headdress. According to Charles Hanson, the auctioneer, Oliver was a complex individual who had a colorful past. At the age of 16, he ran away and ended up on a ship to Canada, where he found work as a lumberjack. He later joined the Staffordshire Police and was known for being a humorous but firm and strict officer. Oliver also owned and ran a pub in Hartington, Derbyshire, before the war. The sale of the collection is scheduled for 25 July.

The Hague - An international arbitration court has awarded Slovenia victory in a long-standing maritime dispute with Croatia, allowing it direct access to international waters in the Adriatic Sea. The Permanent Court of Arbitration's ruling is final and binding, but Croatia, which withdrew from the proceedings in 2015, has stated it will disregard the decision. According to the court, Slovenia should have uninterrupted access to the sea it shares with Croatia. The decision comes in a case between EU neighbours. Croatian Prime Minister Andrej Plenkovic has expressed his country's refusal to implement the ruling, saying they are "open to a bilateral dialogue with Slovenia and do not expect any one-sided action on this issue." Slovenia's government welcomed the ruling, calling it "definitive and legally binding". Slovenian Prime Minister Miro Cerar stated that Slovenia will continue good cooperation with Croatia and will not take any actions that could worsen relations. The countries have been disputing a stretch of their shared sea and land border since both gained independence from Yugoslavia in 1991. The dispute, focusing on the bay of Piran, previously hindered Croatia's EU accession. Both parties agreed to arbitration, which granted Zagreb EU membership in 2013. The court has now ruled that Slovenia will control the majority of the Piran bay area as its territorial waters, and established a 2.5 nautical-mile wide corridor through Croatian waters, allowing for direct access to international waters. The ruling also guarantees freedom of communication to all ships and aircraft of any state for the purpose of access to Slovenia. Croatia withdrew from the arbitration process in 2015 after a leaked tape revealed a Slovenian judge improperly exchanging confidential information with the Ljubljana government. The judge involved resigned, and the court decided to proceed with the case, stating that the incident did not compromise its ability to reach a final verdict. Slovenia insists that Croatia should respect the verdict, while Croatian officials believe the issue should be resolved bilaterally. The EU is looking to this arbitration between Croatia and Slovenia as a model for handling other border disputes involving Balkan EU hopefuls. However, Croatia's unilateral withdrawal raises questions about the success of future arbitrations and whether promises made to secure EU membership will be kept.
REC Silicon to Miss Q3 Polysilicon Production, Sales Forecast REC Silicon ASA reported on Friday that it does not expect to meet its previous guidance for third-quarter polysilicon production and sales. The company attributes this to the ongoing solar trade war between the US and China, as well as a decline in photovoltaic market conditions. As a result, REC Silicon will operate at roughly 50% of full capacity at its Moses Lake facility in Washington by October 1, 2016. Production is expected to slow until market conditions improve. The company now projects Q3 polysilicon sales volumes, excluding fines and powders, to reach 1,800 tonnes. July-September revenues are forecasted to range between USD 45 million (EUR 40m) and USD 50 million, a decrease from USD 71.1 million in the prior quarter due to lower Fluidised Bed Reactor sales volumes. REC Silicon forecasts Q3 total polysilicon production volumes to reach 3,900 tonnes, falling short of its previous guidance of 4,490 tonnes. FBR production is expected at 3,300 tonnes, versus a prior projection of 3,830 tonnes. The company is also in talks with its joint venture partner to delay its second and third capital contributions, totaling USD 169 million, needed for the construction of a FBR polysilicon plant in Yulin, China. These contributions will not be made until the trade war is resolved.
A Phillips Exeter Academy minister asked a male student accused of sexual misconduct to bake bread for his alleged victim as an act of penance, according to The Boston Globe. This unusual arrangement, reported by the Globe's Spotlight team, is part of a broader examination of how elite New England boarding schools handle sexual misconduct on campus. In May, the Globe revealed that a Phillips Exeter teacher and administrator, who had won awards, had admitted to decades-old sexual misconduct but had kept it secret from students and alumni. However, these questions are not just about past indiscretions. Last fall, 17-year-old Michaella Henry reported that a male student, Chukwudi "Chudi" Ikpeazu, had inappropriately touched her despite her repeated "no." Instead of reporting the incident to the authorities, school Rev. Robert Thompson gathered Ikpeazu and Henry to work out their differences. Out of this meeting came an agreement that Ikpeazu would bake a weekly serving of "monkey bread" and deliver it to Henry. The minister also pressured Ikpeazu to bake bread and deliver it to Henry for the rest of the year as an act of penance. Rev. Thompson praised Michaella for accepting the arrangement, writing that she "gave Chudi an opportunity to express his regret and take responsibility for what he had done." However, this arrangement added to Henry's stress, forcing her to meet with Ikpeazu weekly. She eventually reported the incident to the police in the spring, and Ikpeazu is set to face arraignment on a misdemeanor charge of sexual assault in August.
Graduates of the class of 2015 left college with an average debt of $30,000, a 4% increase from the previous year, according to a report by the Institute for College Access and Success. The organization's president, Lauren Asher, stated, "We need to make college more affordable and reduce the burden of debt for students and families." California had the third lowest average debt, at $22,000. However, the state's debt levels are rising at a similar rate to the nation as a whole. The top California college with the highest debt was National University, where graduates left with nearly $53,000 in debt. Student debt at the University of California campuses ranged from $17,869 at U.C. Berkeley to $22,580 at U.C. Santa Cruz. At California State University campuses, debt levels varied from $10,872 at Fresno State to $23,973 at Humboldt State. The institute acknowledged a gap in its report, as it only includes data from non-profit colleges, which often do not disclose student debt. Diane Cheng, associate research director, noted that actual state averages may be higher than reported, as some colleges do not report data and students may have unreported private loans. The institute has also obtained data from the U.S. Department of Education, which showed that in 2012, graduates from for-profit colleges had an average debt of around $40,000. The report suggests that states consider using financial need as the primary factor when awarding grants to college students, notify students about their loans to help them make informed decisions, and require colleges to inform students about untapped federal aid before approving private loan requests.

The Department of Justice is urging the Census Bureau to include a question about citizenship status on 2020 census forms, according to a letter released last Friday. The December 12 letter from DOJ lawyer Arthur Gary to Census Bureau official Dr. Ron Jarmin argued that the bureau should include the citizenship question as part of enforcing the Voting Rights Act. "In order to fully enforce those requirements, the Department needs a reliable calculation of the citizen voting-age population in localities where voting rights violations are suspected or alleged," the letter stated. The Census Bureau acknowledged the letter's existence, saying that the request would go through the established process for any potential question. This letter comes as several recent reports have hinted that the Trump administration had planned to include an immigration status question in the 2020 census. Critics warn that including an immigration-related question could lead to a "chilling effect" on the Census response rate, while supporters believe it would help ensure the integrity of future elections.

Following his departure from Hamburg in the summer, Tavares became available on a free transfer.

Bill Gates announced that the Bill & Melinda Gates Foundation will increase its funding to combat malaria, aiming to spend over $200 million annually. This is part of the foundation's broader plan to tackle tropical diseases, with a total commitment of more than $500 million this year to address various illnesses, including pneumonia, diarrhea, and parasitic diseases in low-income countries. Gates expressed his confidence that malaria can be eradicated within his lifetime. He also stated that the foundation plans to develop a treatment or vaccine for individuals carrying the disease without showing symptoms. The foundation's efforts include a $156 million grant to the PATH Malaria Vaccine Initiative, which will support the creation of new vaccines to disrupt the malarial parasite's transmission cycle. PATH's president and CEO, Steve Davis, said the grant will help ensure the organization's efforts to implement a strategy aimed at controlling and eventually eradicating malaria. In addition to malaria, the Gates foundation has pledged $50 million for research on Ebola treatments, tests, and vaccines. Despite some countries and groups contributing to Ebola efforts, Gates emphasized the need for a larger, sustained response to the outbreak, which has claimed around 5,000 lives in eight countries this year. He warned that a more transmissible epidemic could occur in the next few decades and called on countries to strengthen their healthcare systems and invest in new treatments and vaccines.

You may already be aware that Near Field Communications can be used for digital wallets and device pairing, but did you know that it can also be harnessed to generate power? Before you cancel your electricity service, rest assured that the amount of power it produces is only enough for a small E Ink display. This was discovered by Liliputing on the NFC Brief site, and while it may seem gimmicky, I can see potential for practical applications. E Ink displays require power only when their screens are refreshed to show new information, which makes this technology particularly useful. For instance, if you have important data on an NFC-enabled smartphone, you could tap the handset to a special E Ink display, wirelessly providing both the data and the power to display it. Check out this example video to see the concept in action. The special NFC tag was jointly developed by Intel Labs, the University of Washington, and the University of Massachusetts Amherst. Although there isn't a commercial product available yet, the concept and demo are compelling. Imagine having companion displays in your car, on your desk, or even built into the backs of laptop bags, where you could show static but useful information without needing more power.
A schoolboy's hands raised in class reveals a surprising connection between children's math skills and their weight. According to a new study, obese kids are more likely to struggle with math than their slimmer peers. Anxiety can also affect math abilities, with women's brains working harder than men's. Kids are more likely to be active if their friends are. Researchers analyzed data from over 6,250 children from a government study that tracks kindergartners through fifth grade. The study found that children who were obese from kindergarten through fifth grade performed poorly on math tests by first grade, compared to their non-obese classmates. Boys who became obese later in elementary school did not experience a decline in math skills, but girls who became obese at later ages showed a temporary drop. Obesity negatively affected children beyond their math abilities, causing them to have fewer social skills and report feeling sadder, lonelier, and more anxious. The study's author, Sara Gable, notes that childhood obesity can harm children's social and emotional well-being and academic performance. Experts are divided on whether obesity causes social, emotional, and academic problems or if the issues arise from a combination of factors. Dr. Becky Hashim, a clinical child psychologist, suggests that obesity can weaken social skills due to social isolation or stigma, while also noting that poor social skills can lead to feelings of sadness and food cravings.
Rats have invaded villages in southern Myanmar, prompting authorities to offer locals a small payment for each rodent they kill. The infestation has been tackled with homemade weapons such as sticks, slingshots, and rocks. Locals claim to have already killed over 4,000 rodents, but concerns remain about the potential for disease. However, villagers are also worried that this plague may be a warning sign of more disasters to come. According to local tradition, these animals are believed to predict bad weather, and some people are concerned about the possibility of floods or earthquakes. A study by Japanese scientists suggests that rats may be sensitive to electromagnetic waves that occur before earthquakes. The rats' bodies have been sent for testing, but so far, no diseases have been detected. Heavy rain in the Ayeyarwady region is thought to be the cause of the infestation, which has destroyed large amounts of food. This is not the first time a massive rat plague has threatened villages in Myanmar. In 2008, thousands of people in the Chin State were left at risk of starvation after the rodents appeared and began eating bamboo fruits and food crops. The phenomenon occurs every 50 years, with the last major outbreak in the 1950s resulting in an estimated 15,000 deaths.

Thirteen states have achieved their lowest ever recorded unemployment rates, a feat not seen since the federal government began tracking state-level data over four decades ago. Eight years after the depths of the 2009 Great Recession, the states experiencing economic booms span the full spectrum, from the most affluent states like Hawaii and California to the most struggling states like Idaho and Texas. In October, a total of seven states – Alabama, Hawaii, Maine, Mississippi, Tennessee, Texas, and Washington – set new records for the lowest unemployment rates ever recorded by the Bureau of Labor Statistics. Other states, including California, Colorado, Idaho, North Dakota, and Oregon, also hit new lows earlier this year. It's a stark contrast to 2010, when six states – California, Colorado, Florida, Georgia, Nevada, and North Carolina – recorded record-high unemployment rates, while Oregon, Rhode Island, and Kansas set their own highs in 2009. Nationally, the unemployment rate stands at 4.1 percent, the lowest level since December 2000, when it reached 3.9 percent. Thirteen states have unemployment rates significantly lower than the national average, while 15 states have rates significantly higher. Hawaii boasts the lowest unemployment rate in the country, at 2.2 percent in October, followed closely by North Dakota at 2.5 percent, and Colorado, Nebraska, and New Hampshire at 2.7 percent each. Alaska, meanwhile, has the highest unemployment rate, at 7.2 percent, followed by the District of Columbia at 6.6 percent, and New Mexico at 6.1 percent. In the last year, Alabama's unemployment rate plummeted the most, by 2.5 percentage points, according to the BLS. Tennessee's unemployment rate dropped 2 percentage points, from 5 percent to 3 percent. Only Alaska, South Dakota, and the District of Columbia have seen their unemployment rates rise in the past 12 months.

Todd worked at a kitchen at the University of Maryland Eastern Shore and had previously asked Somerset County to help pay his heating bill. The county's Office of Home Energy Programs had previously helped Todd, but it's unclear why he didn't apply for assistance this year. The community is left to wonder why Todd didn't seek help when he needed it most.

A formal currency union with the pound is unlikely for an independent Scotland due to hardline conditions set by London, according to a former economic adviser. Professor John Kay, a former member of the Council of Economic Advisers, warned that negotiations over a currency deal would be "intractable" for Scotland. This stance has been echoed by a former chief economist, who believes no UK chancellor would risk taxpayers' funds in such an arrangement. The SNP government's desire to keep the pound in a monetary union with the UK after independence has been met with rejection by Chancellor George Osborne and his Labour counterpart, Ed Balls. Kay stated that the conventional wisdom, particularly in the eurozone, suggests that currency union requires fiscal backing. However, he personally doubts this assertion, acknowledging that it's widely believed by markets and politicians. The potential for negotiations to fail is high, as the UK Treasury would likely impose conditions that Scotland would be unwilling to accept. The rest of the UK would demand control over Scotland's banking system and fiscal policy, which Scotland would not be willing to concede. If Scotland agreed to the UK's demands, it would be giving away most of the economic policy levers it sought to gain by independence. Gavin McCrone, a former chief economist at the Scottish Office, expressed skepticism about a chancellor being prepared to put taxpayers at risk in the rest of the country for Scotland's debt or bad debt. He believes this is the main reason why George Osborne and others are hesitant to contemplate currency union. Despite this, negotiations would likely take place.

New Delhi: The Supreme Court has referred the issue of fixed dose combination (FDC) drugs to the government's expert body, the Drugs Technical Advisory Board (DTAB), for a fresh review of their safety, efficacy, and therapeutic justification. The court ordered that the DTAB or a sub-committee constituted by it should examine all stakeholders and forward its report to the government for action within six months. However, the court excluded 15 FDCs that were licensed prior to 1988 from its order. It also instructed the government to maintain the status quo for the remaining 329 FDCs being referred to DTAB for review. The All India Drugs Action Network welcomed the order, saying it clears the way for the government to take steps to eliminate large numbers of irrational, unscientific, and hazardous FDCs prevalent in India. According to the network, the 344 FDCs that were banned account for only about 5% of the total FDCs in India, with roughly half considered irrational. The network urged the government to capitalize on this opportunity to remove other irrational FDCs, prioritizing patient safety. Pfizer Ltd, the Indian unit of US-based Pfizer, expressed support for the government's goal of eradicating irrational combinations and medicines not approved by state and central regulators through a consultative process. In January, the Centre had filed an appeal against a 2016 Delhi high court ruling that quashed the Centre's 2016 notification banning 344 FDC drugs due to health risks and lack of therapeutic justification. The Supreme Court had stayed proceedings in all high courts against the ban on 344 FDC drugs in March. An FDC drug contains two or more active ingredients in a fixed dosage ratio. The ban on 344 FDC drugs covered about 6,000 brands from major pharmaceutical companies, including Pfizer Ltd, Wockhardt Ltd, Alkem Laboratories Ltd, Cipla Ltd, Sanofi India Ltd, and Sun Pharmaceutical Industries Ltd. The ban was enforced after a report by a six-member committee headed by Chandrakant Kokate, vice-chancellor of KLE University, Karnataka, which identified 963 FDCs as "irrational" and posing health threats. A Delhi high court judge had quashed the notification, holding that the government had failed to consult statutory authorities like DTAB and the Drugs Consultative Committee before the ban.
Britain's economy is expected to lose momentum in the second half of 2017, according to a closely watched survey that may disappoint some Bank of England officials who are eager to raise interest rates for the first time in a decade. The survey found that the UK services sector experienced a four-month low in growth in June, with the Markit/CIPS index dipping to 53.4. This is down from 53.8 in May and just shy of the forecast 53.5. The survey also showed that business expectations have hit a nine-month low, with growth in new orders falling to its lowest level since last July. This was partly due to uncertainty following the UK's general election in June, as well as Brexit talks and economic concerns. The Bank of England's rate-setter Michael Saunders had argued that lower consumer spending would be offset by higher exports and investment, but the latest survey suggests otherwise. JPMorgan economist Allan Monks said the weakness in the UK PMI comes at a time when the broader European PMIs have strengthened considerably. The slowdown in the economy is also reflected in car sales, which fell for a third month in June, albeit from recent record highs. Productivity, a major economic issue in Britain, also fell in the first three months of the year, the first decline since late 2015. This raises concerns for policymakers, as weak productivity can lead to lower wage growth and higher inflation.

A recently declassified State Department report revealed that India was capable of developing nuclear weapons as early as 1964. This report, along with others published on May 18 by the National Security Archive and the Nuclear Proliferation International History Project, highlighted India's potential nuclear ambitions. According to the Press Trust of India, the report pointed to frequent changes in the fuel core of the Canadian-Indian Reactor (CIR) at Trombay, which occurred every six months. At the time, US intelligence had raised concerns about India's nuclear goals. The State Department Bureau of Intelligence and Research (INR) stated in the report, "The Indians are now in a position to begin nuclear weapons development if they chose to do so." However, the INR also noted that there was no evidence of a dedicated nuclear weapons research and development program. The report raised concerns due to the short timeframe for "normal research reactor operations," suggesting that six months was an ideal time for producing weapons-grade plutonium. Despite the INR report stating that there was no evidence of a nuclear bomb program for India, it acknowledged that India's actions so far were "suitable to building a weapons programme in the future." The State Department report suggested that India's leadership might have had nationalistic motives for building the Phoenix plant, but if they sought a nuclear weapons capability, they would pursue it. The report concluded that India had taken a "deliberate decision" to pursue a nuclear weapon, meaning they had access to and the ability to produce or obtain weapons-grade plutonium. By 2013, India was estimated to have at least 110 nuclear weapons. Notably, the country has signed and ratified the Biological Weapons Convention and the Chemical Weapons Convention but has not signed the Nuclear Non-Proliferation Treaty due to concerns about the treaty's implications on the nuclear arsenals of other countries, including the US, Russia, China, the UK, and France.

A new motorway between Gort and Tuam in Co Galway has opened, stretching 57km and costing almost €500m. The toll-free M17/M18 is expected to slash journey times to and from the northwest by bypassing several traffic hotspots. After nearly a decade and a half of planning, the motorway has been under construction for several years. The new route is set to significantly reduce congestion in towns like Tuam, Claregalway, and Clarinbridge, which motorists will no longer need to navigate. However, concerns have been raised that problems in these areas will be redirected towards Galway city, where traffic congestion is already a major issue. In response, Transport Infrastructure Ireland and Galway County Council are viewing today's opening as part of a broader strategy to tackle increased traffic volumes. The next phase will involve the construction of a Galway city bypass, but proposals for this project are already contentious in the areas that will be affected, and it is likely to face opposition when it goes to the planning stage in the coming months.

Despite the El Nino winter, California remains in a drought. In Marin County, water restrictions are still in place, but the drought appears to be mostly a formality. Six of seven reservoirs are considered full, and the one that's not is 95% capacity. The drought persists, as does the El Nino condition, across the state. The Marin Municipal Water District reports 98% capacity in its reservoirs, a relatively healthy picture compared to the rest of California. Crystal Yezman, who manages the Tamalpais watershed, attributes Marin County's near-capacity status to residents' continued efforts to reduce water use. Yezman notes that Marin County's reservoirs are uniquely full, even earning a third layer of fish, Coho salmon. Fishery program manager Gregory Andrew spotted and counted one of the 500 Coho salmon that returned to Lagunitas Creek this year, the best showing in a decade. Early, well-spaced storms allowed the Coho to swim upstream in December, a perfect condition for the fish. However, Andrew reassures that the Coho population on Lagunitas Creek remains sustainable, albeit precarious.
Researchers have discovered that the medicinal herb Rhus javanica possesses oral therapeutic anti-herpes simplex virus (HSV) activity in mice. The scientists isolated two main anti-HSV compounds, moronic acid and betulonic acid, from the herb using a combination of extraction and chromatographic techniques. They tested these compounds for their anti-HSV activity in laboratory settings and found that moronic acid was the most potent, with an effective concentration of 3.9 micrograms per milliliter. Moronic acid also had a higher therapeutic index than betulonic acid, indicating its greater safety and efficacy. Notably, moronic acid showed similar effectiveness against strains of HSV that were resistant to acyclovir, a commonly used antiviral medication. In a mouse model, moronic acid was administered orally three times a day to mice infected with HSV-1 and found to significantly slow the development of skin lesions and extend their survival times without causing any adverse effects. Moronic acid was more effective at reducing virus yields in the brain than in the skin, which is consistent with its ability to prolong survival times. Overall, moronic acid was identified as a major anti-HSV compound from the herbal extract of Rhus javanica, offering a novel approach to treating HSV infections. Its mode of action differs from that of acyclovir, and it demonstrates oral therapeutic efficacy in infected mice.
A new law aimed at reducing drunk driving has been signed into effect by the governor, which could lead to tougher penalties for repeat offenders. Under the legislation, drivers who accumulate three or more DUI convictions within a decade could face the loss of their license for up to 10 years. This stricter approach is a significant change from the current law, which allows judges to revoke a driver's license for only three years in such cases. The law, sponsored by Assemblyman Jerry Hill, is set to take effect on January 1, 2012. Hill believes that this measure could help remove over 10,000 repeat offenders from the road each year. In 2008, nearly 188,000 DUI convictions were handed down in the state, with 9,164 of those drivers facing their third DUI charge. The National Highway Traffic Safety Administration estimates that around one-third of the DUI arrests in California each year involve repeat offenders. The agency reports that more than 310,000 Californians have three or more DUI convictions. Hill urges judges to use this new authority to remove repeat DUI offenders from the road. Governor Arnold Schwarzenegger, a Republican, also welcomed the legislation, stating that it is an important step towards making California's roads safer.
Abnormal behavior in animals can be defined in various ways. For instance, statistically, it occurs when the frequency or intensity of a behavior deviates significantly from what's considered normal. This means that almost any behavior could be deemed abnormal in an individual. Alternatively, 'abnormal' behavior is also characterized as any activity that falls outside the typical pattern of behavior for an animal of a specific class or age. For example, infanticide might be a normal behavior in one species, but it becomes abnormal if it becomes too frequent in another species. The list of abnormal behaviors doesn't include one-time actions by individual animals, unless these behaviors are repeated by other animals in the species and are recognized as part of the species' ethogram. Most abnormal behaviors can be broadly categorized into types such as eliminative, ingestive, and stereotypic behaviors. However, many abnormal behaviors don't fit neatly into one category, and categorization is not attempted here. Some abnormal behaviors are linked to environmental factors, such as captive housing conditions, while others are caused by medical conditions. This list doesn't include behaviors exhibited by genetically modified animals that display abnormal behavior. Examples of abnormal behaviors include a polar bear performing stereotyped pacing and an Asiatic elephant exhibiting stereotyped rocking and trunk swinging.

The way a retail store is set up is a subtle balance of strategic spatial decisions. Placing essentials like toilet paper or milk at the back of the store, out of sight, forces shoppers to navigate through higher-margin products like clothing or toys before reaching the items they need. Stores are typically arranged to be navigated in a clockwise direction, making it easy for right-handed shoppers to push carts and grab items from shelves with their dominant hand. Many stores have a subtle scent, as research has shown that pleasant smells can increase impulsivity in consumers. However, as shoppers become more focused on what they want to buy, retailers' tactics are becoming less effective. According to a retail consultant, "Consumers are now conditioned to shop for specific items, not just online but also in-store, and this is affecting how they shop in both environments." This shift has led to consumers buying only what they need, ignoring other products, and then leaving the store. As a result, retailers are struggling to adapt without relying on tactics that have been successful for decades. One way consumers are coping is by setting rules for themselves. A study by The Wall Street Journal tracked the shopping habits of Wisconsinites in a grocery store and found that some couples shop together, allowing them to monitor each other's impulses. Others avoid using shopping carts, fearing they'll feel pressured to buy more.

The blaze, which started in a shanty house in the Tondo district, left seven residents injured as they desperately tried to salvage their belongings. Despite efforts to determine the cause of the blaze, it is suspected to be related to faulty electrical wiring, a common issue in the area where many homes have illicit connections.
Fully accomplished Dzogchen practitioners have the ability to dissolve their physical body at the time of death. Through the practice of trekchö, a practitioner can attain a state known as the 'rainbow body', where their body gradually shrinks and is replaced by a brilliant rainbow light. In this state, only their hair and nails remain. The practice of tögal allows a practitioner to dissolve their body into a state of complete lightness, where they disappear into space. This phenomenon has been observed in several notable figures, including Garab Dorje, Manjushrimitra, Shri Singha, Jnanasutra, and Vairotsana. One of the accomplishments of tögal practice is the 'Rainbow Body of Great Transference', where a master dissolves their body into rainbow light and lives for centuries to benefit others. This is seen in the cases of Padmasambhava, Vimalamitra, Nyang Tingdzin Zangpo, and Chetsün Senge Wangchuk.

Depending on your specific needs, MongoDB version 3.4 offers a powerful aggregation pipeline operator called $graphLookup. This operator can perform a recursive search on a collection. For more detailed information, see the $graphLookup definition. To illustrate how this operator works, let's use the following example. Suppose you have a collection with a hierarchy defined by documents. You could try running the following aggregation pipeline: ```javascript db.collectionName.aggregate([ { $unwind: { path: "$childrenIdList", preserveNullAndEmptyArrays: true } }, { $graphLookup: { from: "collectionName", startWith: "$_id", connectFromField: "_id", connectToField: "childrenIdList", as: "myparents", restrictSearchWithMatch: { "_id": 7 } } }, { $match: { "_id": 7 } }, { $group: { _id: "$_id", parents: { $addToSet: "$myparents._id" } } } ]); ``` The result of this query should be: ``` { "_id" : 7, "parents" : [ 1, 2, 4 ] } ``` However, if you have a large collection, this query may not be efficient, as it involves unwinding each document and doesn't take advantage of indexes. As others have suggested, it's worth reconsidering your document model's structure. For more information, see Data Models - Tree Structures. Ultimately, optimize based on your application's logic and querying use case, and let the flexible document schema adapt to your needs.

The shooting occurred just days after Brown, an unarmed 18-year-old African American, was fatally shot by Officer Darren Wilson in Ferguson, Missouri. Critics and news outlets questioned why the Ferguson police released an incident report from a robbery in which Brown was a suspect, as well as security video showing the robbery, but not the report on the shooting. The St. Louis County prosecutor's office revealed that no incident report for the shooting existed, as the case was turned over to the county police department almost immediately. According to officials from the office of St. Louis County Prosecuting Attorney Robert P. McCulloch, the reason for this lack of documentation was that it simply didn't exist. The St. Louis County police department presumably did file an incident report, but any such documents will not be made public until a grand jury investigating the officer-involved shooting concludes its investigation. A grand jury reviewing the case is currently impaneled until mid-September, but it could continue to deliberate beyond its term, focusing solely on the shooting of Brown. The evidence, compiled from eyewitness accounts and DigitalGlobe satellite imagery, paints a grim picture of "systematic mass killing of civilians" in Kadugli, South Kordofan. TIME was the first to break the news of Clooney's initiative. The project combines eyewitness testimony with satellite imagery to pinpoint areas of suspected mass graves and killings, including piles of bodies and mass graves. The report cites four eyewitness accounts of Sudan Armed Forces and northern Sudanese militias searching homes in Kadugli, killing civilians suspected of supporting southern Sudan forces. The accounts describe gruesome scenes, including the slitting of a civilian's throat and the sealing and burning of homes with civilians inside. Eyewitnesses also describe the mass graves, which were dug by a yellow earth mover near the Tilo School in Kadugli, just a mile away. The graves are approximately 26 meters long and 5 meters wide, and large green trucks were seen unloading around 100 bodies at the site. Witnesses claim that before being buried in the mass grave, some of the bodies were wrapped in white plastic and piled up in Kadugli, with the Satellite Sentinel Project capturing a pile of those bodies.

This latest incident is also a blow to Thailand's reputation, which has been marred by recent disclosures about corrupt officials and human trafficking. In June, the US placed Thailand in its lowest category - Tier 3 - in its annual assessment of human trafficking efforts. Thailand has vowed to take action to avoid being blacklisted, but its reputation has suffered from recent revelations about forced labour on Thai fishing vessels. The investigation will continue to expand to other areas with dense jungle cover. A survivor from the camp has confirmed that smugglers escaped with around 100 Rohingya, and police are working to confirm reports of more camps. The Rohingya have faced decades of state-sanctioned discrimination in Myanmar, where they are a minority. Mob attacks in the past three years have claimed up to 280 lives, prompting a massive exodus.

The free movement of labor is a vital component of the European project and a crucial element in the functioning of the monetary union. In light of this theme and the current debate, we've created four informative charts to illustrate the topic. Last month, Bruegel organized an event that explored migration in the EU and its impact on society and the economy. This event was inspired by the current political debate and highlighted the importance of labor mobility. Net migration rates per 1,000 inhabitants in Europe in 2012 are presented in the charts. According to Bruegel's analysis based on Eurostat data, the rates vary significantly across EU countries. For instance, Germany and Belgium had high net inflows of 4.3 and 6.5 migrants per 1,000 inhabitants, while Spain and Greece experienced net outflows of -3 and -4, indicating more people leaving than arriving. Unemployment and net migration are also closely linked. The charts show that countries with higher unemployment rates tend to have lower net migration rates. Furthermore, countries with worse economic health tend to experience larger net outflows of people, and those leaving often migrate to countries with better economic prospects. The main destinations in Core Europe are identified by examining population breakdowns by country of citizenship in 2013. The chart shows that the countries on the right and left are the main senders, while those in the center are the main hosts. Labor mobility not only plays a crucial role in macroeconomic stability but also benefits the micro level by improving potential firm-worker matching, addressing skills shortages, and fostering international commerce by reducing cultural barriers to trade.

Iraq is currently facing its most severe security crisis since US troops withdrew in 2011. ISIL, a splinter of Iraq's al-Qaeda group, has taken control of a significant portion of the country's north and west, following its capture of Mosul, Iraq's second-largest city, and most of the western Anbar province last year. The militant group has been carrying out attacks against government forces, and now controls around a third of Iraq and neighbouring Syria within its self-declared "caliphate". Since its emergence, Baghdad and other major cities have seen near-daily violence, including roadside bombs, suicide blasts, and assassinations targeting Iraqi forces and government officials, resulting in significant casualties among the civilian population. The violence has claimed hundreds of lives and displaced tens of thousands of Iraqis.

One way to do this is to set up environment variables using batch files provided by Visual Studio. You can create a batch file that sets these variables and then runs the VS batch file to set them. This approach requires some setup, but it's doable. For example, you can create a batch file called `vc2013.bat` that calls the `vcvars32.bat` file to set the environment variables. Then, from within Emacs, you can use the `compile` command to run `vc2013.bat` followed by your C++ command. I'm new to C++ and would appreciate any tips on how to integrate Emacs with Visual Studio. What can be done, what shouldn't be done, and what's the current state of the art? I've found some old links that suggest using Emacs 19, which is over 10 years old. In my experience, I only use the Visual Studio IDE for debugging, which is rare. A portable breathalyzer company, BACtrack, has released data from nearly 300,000 breathalyzer tests taken nationwide in 2014. Some results aren't surprising - the most intoxicated days of the year are typically St. Patrick's Day and New Year's Eve. What's more surprising is that Waltham, Massachusetts had the highest average blood alcohol concentration (BAC) in the US during December. BACtrack's consumption report reveals that 14 out of the top 15 drinking days occur in the winter months - the only exception being May 3rd, which fell on the weekend before Cinco de Mayo. Besides obvious picks like New Year's Eve and Super Bowl Sunday, the day after Valentine's Day saw an unusually high BAC, with a reading of 0.092, possibly due to heartbroken singles seeking solace in alcohol. In a city-by-city breakdown, Waltham had the highest recorded BAC for December, beating out nearby Jersey City, New Jersey, and other cities. So, is Waltham really the most intoxicated city in America? Probably not. To put this into perspective, while 300,000 breathalyzer measurements nationwide may sound impressive, breaking down the data shows how limited the sample size truly is. Assuming an average of 6,000 breathalyzer measurements per state, Waltham, with a relatively small population, would account for a disproportionately large number of samples. For instance, if Massachusetts collected 12,000 samples, and Waltham's population is less than 1% of the state's, it's likely that Waltham contributed more than its fair share. Even with 20 measurements in December, this is still a tiny sample, and it's unlikely that the average person would use a breathalyzer every hour. With the highest recorded BAC being 0.133%, it's likely that only a few people were responsible for this reading. The moral of the story is to look beyond the numbers and consider the context. While Waltham residents may be enjoying the holiday season, it's essential to drink responsibly and use a designated driver to avoid any potential issues.

California is closer to having a third presidential primary after the state Senate voted overwhelmingly in favor of a bill to schedule primary votes in March. Senate Bill 568, one of two bills being considered this year, would shift the state's primary from June to March, a move that could make California one of the first states to hold a presidential primary. The bill was approved on a bipartisan 32-6 vote, with State Senator Ricardo Lara, a Democrat from Bell Gardens, authoring it. Lara argued that California should be at the table to influence national decisions, citing the state's leadership in clean energy, farming, job growth, and diversity. In a written statement, Lara stated that the Prime Time Primary Bill would enable California voters to participate in the national debate and give their state a stronger voice in presidential elections.
Arkansas officials must recognize over 500 same-sex marriages performed last year, a ruling that will allow couples to enjoy benefits like filing taxes together. Pulaski County Circuit Judge Wendell Griffen validated marriage licenses for same-sex couples on Tuesday, following another judge's decision to strike down the state's gay marriage ban. The Arkansas Supreme Court had previously halted the distribution of marriage licenses to gay couples in May 2014, but Griffen's decision means the couples can now enjoy a range of rights, including joint tax filing, state health insurance coverage, and joint appearance on a child's birth certificate. However, the state can still appeal Griffen's ruling. For more information on this story, visit our affiliate station's website, KTHV - Channel 11.
For the next 10 days, leading up to the start of training camp on July 28, The Baltimore Sun is breaking down the Ravens' roster position by position. The countdown begins with the least competitive positions and ends with the most challenging. We've already examined the quarterback, defensive line, offensive line, tight ends, and inside linebackers. Today, we'll focus on cornerbacks. The team is likely to keep six cornerbacks, with Jimmy Smith, Shareece Wright, and Jerraud Powers considered locks if they remain healthy. However, Kyle Arrington, Will Davis, Maurice Canady, and Sheldon Price are on the bubble, while Julian Wilson and Sam Brown are considered long shots. Jumal Rolle is currently on injured reserve due to an Achilles injury. Given the Ravens' struggles with cornerbacks' health in recent seasons, they'll likely keep as many cover guys as possible, even if they need to stash a few on the practice squad. The group heading into training camp includes a mix of youth and experience, with Smith and Wright, who were high school teammates, expected to start on the outside. Powers, a recent free-agent signing from the Arizona Cardinals, has the edge in the slot, thanks to his constant involvement in the team's mandatory minicamp. Young and Canady, both rookies, are also expected to make the team, although their field time will depend on their performance in training camp and the preseason. This leaves room for only one or two additional cornerbacks from the group that includes Arrington, Davis, Price, and Wilson. Arrington, who took a pay cut to stay with the Ravens, will need to prove he's a better player than he was last season. Davis, who is highly valued by the team, will also need to show he can stay healthy. Price and Wilson, who both have the physical attributes to succeed in a secondary that lacks size, will be tested this summer and have a chance to stay with the organization.

Since many of us already use this size of keyboard, I think it would be a good idea to include these or an extra extension set for 75% keyboards. The extension set would include the above six, plus the Arrows (R4) and the Win/CTRL/ALT on the left side. The 75% keys will be included in the base set, as mentioned in the original post. SKIDATA+ will be following the conventional Cherry 75% layout, which is (from top to bottom) Home, PgUp, PgDn, End. I'm not sure what you mean by arrows + Win/CTRL/ALT on the left, but rest assured that these keys will be included in the base set, regardless of whether it's a Winkeyless or Winkey size. The base set will include keys for 1800, HHKB, 75%, and some extras, all in Skidata colours. There won't be many keys that you'll be missing from the base set. Don't worry, as a keyboard enthusiast, my intention has always been to offer a Skidata keyset for the community, with enough keys to fit every conventional Cherry-style keyboard out there. Unfortunately, there are some weird keyboards that use unconventional layouts, making it impossible to support those unusual key sizes. It will become clearer once the mockups are posted, so please look forward to that.

Recently released documents before the Church's Family Synod failed to deliver on hopes of easing its anti-gay stance, raising concerns that the Church is becoming increasingly out of touch. Plans to engage with gay couples that were abandoned last year after a public embarrassment to the Pope have been put on hold once again, despite speculation that similar initiatives might resurface this year. However, a working paper released ahead of this year's synod does not mention reaching out to homosexual couples as a key topic. Although no concrete plans for outreach or policy relaxation are on the agenda for the gathering of Catholic bishops at the Vatican in October, the document does emphasize the importance of "respect" in its "Pastoral attention to persons with homosexual tendencies." It states, "Every person, regardless of their sexual orientation, is respected for their dignity and should be treated with sensitivity and care, both within the church and in society." The document also suggests that diocesan projects should prioritize supporting families and individuals with "homosexual tendencies." A four-member Pakistani delegation is set to arrive in India on Sunday to kick off a three-day official visit to the Sabarmati Riverfront Development Project (SRDP). The delegation, led by Lahore Commissioner Rashid Mehmood Langrial, includes representatives from the Lahore Development Authority (LDA) and a technical expert on urban infrastructure projects. According to a Punjab government official, the LDA has initiated work on a related project, the Ravi Riverfront Urban Development Project (RRUDP), with the assistance of a foreign consultancy firm, and the delegation aims to study the SRDP and replicate it in Lahore. The visit was initially scheduled for the second week of May but was postponed due to officials' prior commitments. However, Prime Minister Nawaz Sharif's interest in the SRDP, sparked after learning about it, has now led to the delegation's trip. Sharif had previously asked officials to visit India, citing the SRDP as a model for Lahore's development. A recent meeting reinforced the visit, with Sharif urging officials to travel to India immediately to brief him on the project. The delegation will enter India through the Wagah Border and arrive in Amritsar, from where they will take a flight to New Delhi. The SRDP is a significant development initiative undertaken by Indian Prime Minister Narendra Modi during his tenure as chief minister of Gujarat.
Louisiana Lawmakers to Explore Marijuana Legalization Options in Bayou State Lawmakers in Louisiana will convene later this month to examine the feasibility and potential benefits of marijuana legalization in the state. The House Criminal Justice Committee has been invited to discuss the matter, although there is currently no pending legislation to legalize marijuana in Louisiana. The state currently has some of the strictest marijuana laws in the country, with penalties that can be severe. Possessing even a small amount of marijuana can result in a jail sentence of up to six months on a first offense, increasing to five years and a $2,500 fine for a second offense, and a mandatory 20-year sentence for a third offense. Last year, a proposal to soften these penalties was passed by the House but fell short in the Senate, with the estimated savings of $2.2 million in reduced incarceration costs for the state in 2014. The sponsor of last year's bill, Representative Austin Badon, has introduced a similar bill for 2014, House Bill 14, which aims to cap jail time for a second marijuana offense at two years and a $500 fine, and subsequent offenses at a maximum of five years in jail and a maximum $2,000 fine. Recent polls have shown that 53% of Louisiana voters support making marijuana legal for adults 21 and older and regulating its sales.

Facebook, the social networking giant, is planning to launch its own smartphone by next year, according to reports. The company has been hiring smartphone engineers and has also launched its own mobile app store, the App Center. Currently, the App Center offers links to Facebook-enabled apps in Apple's iOS and Google Android stores, but developers will soon be able to create apps exclusively for Facebook's store. Experts who worked on the iPhone and other smartphones have been brought in to help with the project. Mark Zuckerberg, Facebook's founder, is reportedly concerned that if he doesn't create a mobile phone soon, Facebook will become just another app on other mobile platforms. Facebook has been struggling to make money from its growing mobile audience, and the company's desire to enter the smartphone market may be a result of increasing pressure to find new ways to monetize mobile users. Facebook's mobile strategy is focused on creating social experiences on every mobile device, and the company is working with various industry partners to achieve this goal.
The Environmental Molecular Sciences Laboratory (EMSL), a national scientific user facility, is dedicated to finding solutions for energy and environmental challenges at the molecular level. Situated at the Pacific Northwest National Laboratory, EMSL is sponsored by the Department of Energy's Office of Science and collaborates with over 800 scientists from academia, government labs, and industry, as well as from nearly all 50 states and other countries annually. EMSL offers both open and proprietary research opportunities and features in-house tools or the ability for researchers to design and build their own specialized instruments. The laboratory's newest high-performance supercomputer, Cascade, is used for a wide range of studies, including the impact of aerosols on water purification and climate projections. Recently, EMSL researchers utilized its unique capabilities, including the Chinook supercomputer, to investigate the types of clouds over the oceans, which are essential for climate forecasting. Current climate models often simplify the variety of clouds that form over the oceans by averaging them into a single type, such as stratocumulus or cumulus clouds, which can cover vast distances. However, distinct cloud types have different effects on the amount of solar energy reaching the ocean surface, potentially introducing errors into large-scale climate models. Researchers at EMSL have confirmed these findings, discovering that climate models averaging a single cloud type significantly underestimate actual ocean cloud cover, leading to overestimations of solar energy reaching the ocean and inaccuracies in predicting temperature variations and movement within the cloud layer. This, in turn, can lead to models predicting a faster transition from stratocumulus to cumulus clouds and introduces uncertainties into climate projections. These discoveries at EMSL could contribute to more accurate climate projections.

The government could implement the GP fee without parliamentary approval, much like it bypassed the parliament to introduce petrol indexation. Health Minister Peter Dutton refused to rule out using a regulation to cut Medicare rebates by $5 to achieve the $3.5 billion in savings outlined in the budget. However, the Australian Medical Association and other key health groups strongly oppose the fee. The government faces a difficult time getting Senate approval for legislation to impose the fee, which is also opposed by the Opposition, the Greens, and the Palmer United Party. AMA president Dr Brian Owler expressed concerns that the government may consider bypassing parliament to introduce the fee, similar to its recent measure to index petrol excise by regulation. Such a move would cut the rebate, taking money away from patients and GPs, and would be detrimental to healthcare. The Medicare rebate is based on a schedule fee set by regulation, and the government can introduce a regulation to slash the current fee by $5 to achieve the desired savings. When asked about the possibility of introducing such a regulation, Health Minister Peter Dutton declined to comment. AMA GP spokesman Dr Brian Morton warned that many GPs would become unviable unless they saw more patients or introduced a $5 charge to make up for the rebate cut. The parliament has the power to disallow any regulation introduced by the government, but if it is introduced in the final sitting in June next year, the measure would come into effect as planned on July 1. However, this could lead to a disallowance motion, which would block the fee cut. The government could use this to gain a one-vote advantage in the Senate, as it only needs 38 votes to block a disallowance motion.
It was a truly great hackathon, as evidenced by this latest report from Patrick Wildt. What we accomplished was substantial. The first major change we made was switching from OABI to EABI for armv7. This is the standard ABI that everyone expects, so we prepared a diff and snapshots beforehand and implemented it during the hackathon. Unfortunately, Zaurus couldn't handle this ABI change, so we ultimately had to remove it from the mix. However, this allowed us to focus on ARMv7 and take advantage of its features, such as using the hardware floating point unit. jsg@ quickly moved armv7 to position and static-positioned code, which will greatly improve C++ exceptions. The next item on our agenda was integrating LLVM and the new C++ stack into the project. With coordinated efforts, I imported libc++, libc++abi, and libunwind, while pascal@ handled the LLVM import. We were able to get everything in place before the hackathon concluded. Now we can move forward and start making it run. While we're making progress, there's still a significant amount of work to be done.
In September of his eighth-grade year, Adam Lanza was consumed by intense anxiety, his mother revealed to doctors. So severe were the feelings that Nancy Lanza took him to Danbury Hospital for an assessment. At 13, Lanza was subjected to standard inquiries by physicians: Was he at risk of harming himself or others? His responses, however, were consistently "no." A 2005 episode documented in medical records suggests a turning point in his middle school years, where his emotional state began to deteriorate more significantly. This episode also raises questions about the impact of his sensory disorder and what some consider to be symptoms of Asperger's syndrome. Seven years later, Lanza would brutally murder his mother and then carry out a deadly rampage at Sandy Hook Elementary School in Newtown. The Hartford Courant has obtained exclusive information from previously secret medical and school records, which cover Lanza's life from birth to age 18. These documents include a September 2005 medical summary of his Danbury Hospital visit, providing new insight into his childhood and adolescence, which had previously appeared relatively uneventful. The period preceding the Danbury Hospital visit was marked by four and a half stable years as a student at Sandy Hook Elementary School, where he would later return as a 20-year-old and brutally slaughter 20 first-graders and six adults, before ultimately taking his own life.
YouTube is finally allowing users to opt-in to its Material Design version on desktop without needing a workaround after over a year of testing. The redesign aims to create a more cohesive experience between its desktop and mobile platforms, with a simpler aesthetic that highlights content. The new design includes features such as infinite scrolling, end-to-end user profile banners, and larger hero videos on profile pages. In theater mode, the search bar at the top of the page turns black, aligning with the rest of the screen. Users can also enable Dark Mode by clicking under their user icon and changing it in settings. A side-by-side comparison image slider allows users to see the differences between Material Design and the classic version. The Material Design update features more white space, a lighter-colored search bar, and aligns the YouTube username under videos with current views. While the preview is currently available to a limited number of users, it will expand once a certain percentage of users have opted-in. According to Manuel Bronstein, VP of product management at YouTube, the redesign will automatically roll out to around 1 percent of users, with plans to expand every few weeks. During testing, around 1 to 3 percent of users experienced the Material Design version. If demand is high, the team will implement the change as quickly as possible. Bronstein noted that there are technical and performance issues that require more time, but hopes the redesign will be ready within a few months. To opt-in to the Material Design preview, users can visit YouTube.com/new. If they're not satisfied with the change, they can revert back to the classic version by clicking "Restore class YouTube" under their accounts menu.

Lin-Manuel Miranda, the creator of the hit Broadway musical "Hamilton," once called a track from the musical "Camelot" "the dopest beat you'll ever hear in your life." He wasn't referring to one of his own songs, but rather a piece from a show his parents introduced him to as a child. Miranda's family didn't often attend Broadway shows, but they collected numerous recordings on vinyl, and he spent hours listening to them. So when it was time to record the cast album for "Hamilton," Miranda was determined to do it justice. In an interview with Charlie Rose, Miranda explained that the album was made for posterity, and that he and the cast were "nailing it" with every song and actor. 60 Minutes producer Graham Messick added that the cast knew the album was for keeps and that they were "just perfect." The magazine filmed the recording session and spoke with Miranda about how he came up with the rapid-fire raps that have made "Hamilton" a huge hit with critics and fans. Sometimes a line would enter Miranda's head and he'd be grateful for it, only to check online to see if anyone else had written it before him. He often joked that he must have stolen it. Given Alexander Hamilton's own way with words, Miranda set a high bar for himself when writing the character's songs. "He needed to be like a world-beating intellect," Miranda said. "So every couplet had to be unimpeachable." The other cast members, including Leslie Odom, Jr., who played Aaron Burr, were also perfectionists. Russia's foreign ministry has cited a factual error in the indictment against Paul Manafort as proof that the allegations are "cooked up" and not part of a serious investigation. Manafort, the former campaign manager of President Donald Trump, and his business associate Rick Gates are accused of charges including conspiracy against the US, money laundering, and being unregistered foreign agents. However, the spokeswoman for Russia's foreign ministry, Maria Zakharova, pointed out that the 31-page indictment incorrectly described Yulia Tymoshenko as a former president of Ukraine. In fact, Tymoshenko served as the country's prime minister twice before being jailed in 2011 on embezzlement charges that the US and others said were politically motivated. Zakharova suggested that the mistake undermined the rest of the indictment, saying it was proof that the document had been "cooked up." She added that such errors were unacceptable in a serious investigation. The Manafort indictment claimed that he and Gates lobbied multiple members of Congress and their staffs about Ukraine sanctions, election validity, and the imprisonment of Yulia Tymoshenko. The indictment also stated that both men generated tens of millions of dollars from their lobbying work in Ukraine. In addition, George Papadopoulos, a former foreign policy adviser to Trump, pleaded guilty to making false statements to the FBI. He is the first person known to be charged and the first to plead guilty in the investigation by special counsel Robert Mueller into the Trump campaign's alleged ties to Russia and Moscow's interference in the election. Russian President Vladimir Putin and other high-ranking government officials have repeatedly denied Moscow's involvement in the vote.
Gmail has recently added an opt-in feature that allows users to send text or SMS messages to mobile phones directly through the built-in Chat functionality. However, this feature has been temporarily put on hold due to a technical issue, and its release is now expected to occur within the next two weeks. In the meantime, an open letter from the Webmail team at AOL expresses its concerns about the potential impact of this feature on users. While the Gmail team claims that the feature is useful, AOL's letter raises several questions about its reliability and professionalism. When enabled in Gmail account settings, this feature enables users to send SMS messages as soon as they start typing a phone number into Chat's search box. Moreover, when new phone numbers are entered, they will be saved in contact entries, allowing users to switch to SMS when contacts go offline. According to a live demo provided by Gmail product manager Keith Coleman, the first time a user sends a text message, it will appear on the recipient's phone as coming from a number in the 406 area code. Google has made thousands of these numbers available for Gmail users, and once associated with an account, all subsequent text messages will come from this number. This 406 number works both ways, allowing recipients to reply via text message and save the number in their phone as belonging to the sender. Users can also initiate new chats with the sender using this number. Although we have not been able to test this feature ourselves, it is listed on the 'What's new in Gmail Labs' page, which is currently available only for US phones. This feature is believed to be one of the first results from Google's acquisition of GrandCentral, which occurred in June 2007. Although there is no official announcement yet, it is likely that an announcement and general roll-out will follow soon.
The final contest of the 2016 Rio Olympics bears a striking resemblance to "Let's Make a Deal." With outstanding debts totaling 100 million reais (US$32 million), the organizing committee is attempting to settle its obligations with goods such as air conditioners, portable energy units, and electrical cables, rather than cash. This financial predicament is a direct result of the financial crisis that struck Brazil at the onset of the Olympics. Rio 2016 is now seeking creditors to agree to accept a 30% reduction in the amount owed, according to Mario Andrada, the committee's head of communications. Andrada expressed hope that the committee will meet its financial obligations by June, when the organizing committee will cease operations. However, if this fails, the burden will be passed on to local and state governments that backed the committee's credit. Unfortunately, these governments are also facing significant financial difficulties, making it unclear whether they can settle the Olympic debts either. The state government, teetering on the brink of bankruptcy, is already struggling to pay public servants. "We are confident that we will come to an agreement and honour our commitments," Andrada said. The committee is still awaiting payment from sponsors. Brazil's economic crisis coincided with the country's largest corruption scandal, resulting in the trial and conviction of prominent business and political leaders, including heads of construction companies that built Olympic-related projects worth approximately $20 billion. Andrada suggested that some of the convicted leaders may be utilizing furniture from the Athletes Village, as mattresses and blankets were sent to a local prison for former police officers. "He's probably sleeping on an Olympic mattress," Andrada quipped. The severe national recession further exacerbated the financial woes of the Olympics, forcing the committee to scale back plans for the opening ceremony, hospitality infrastructure, and other non-essential elements. Emergency public funds were sought to stage the Paralympics, while the IOC contributed a substantial amount, largely before the deadline to help keep the committee afloat. A promise of 250 million reais from local and national governments fell short, amounting to just 90 million reais, and is partly to blame for the failure to pay creditors. The local organizing committee will disband in June 2017.

Healthcare in the U.S. is undeniably pricey. But just how bad is it? Yes. This National Geographic graphic effectively summarizes the three key aspects of the issue: cost, outcomes, and access. If you're unfamiliar with this type of graph, some context is necessary. The left side of the chart displays several countries, arranged on an axis showing their annual per capita healthcare spending. To the right is the average life expectancy of their citizens. The lines that connect the two axes represent a country's healthcare costs and the health of its people. Ideally, you'd want to see a positive correlation between spending and life expectancy, but in the U.S., the lines are more like a flat line, indicating that we're not getting much value for our money. The graphic also highlights the problem of access to healthcare. The thickness of each line indicates how often residents see a doctor, with countries like Japan and the Czech Republic seeming to make it easier for their citizens to access care, while the U.S. struggles to provide similar access.

Does it matter if you feel connected to your community, as long as you have relationships elsewhere? A rare study by Kim and colleagues controlled for social connections at an individual level. "We also controlled for personality traits," Kim explained, "to ensure that optimistic people wouldn't attribute their social connections to their own positivity." The survey included measures of optimism, as well as factors like age, race, income, marital status, education, mental health, and known risk factors for heart disease. When asked if people should get involved in their communities, Kim replied, "I don't think there's enough evidence to support that." "This is just a correlation," he said. "We didn't establish causation. But I don't see how that would be detrimental." Kim suggested that people checking in on each other and sharing health information could contribute to the observed benefits. He also emphasized the importance of emotional support in reducing stress. Researchers like Kim, who focus on the positive aspects of psychology, have found associations between optimism and a reduced risk of heart failure and stroke.
