A network of mentors played a significant role in helping Gordon navigate his journey to becoming the first openly gay male player in Division I basketball. Standing at 6-foot-2, the guard averaged 9.8 points and 4.9 rebounds per game this past season for the Minutemen. Gordon publicly revealed his sexuality in April last year. When asked about his departure, he expressed gratitude towards the coaches and teammates who have been supportive throughout his journey. "I appreciate everything the coaches and my teammates have done for me," he said. "Leaving UMass has absolutely nothing to do with my sexuality - everyone has been incredibly supportive of my situation." The Minutemen made it to the NCAA tournament the previous year but finished the season with a 17-15 overall record and a 10-8 mark in the Atlantic 10. Gordon explained that his decision to leave is a personal one, driven by his desire to find the best situation to succeed. As the US presidential election approaches, the White House is gearing up for a smooth transition between administrations, which involves handing over the President's social media accounts. This includes transferring access to the @POTUS Twitter account, which was launched in May 2015 and now boasts over 11 million followers. However, all tweets will be deleted, allowing the next president to start their social media campaign from a clean slate on January 20. This process also applies to the Presidential Facebook page, Instagram account, YouTube, Medium, and Tumblr accounts. Fortunately, all content created during Obama's presidency will be preserved in partnership with the National Archives and Records Administration (NARA), and will be accessible online through new handles like @POTUS44 on Twitter. Even the current WhiteHouse.gov site will be archived and made viewable at ObamaWhiteHouse.gov, although this website is not yet live. The Obama administration plans to make all its archived content available for public download, and invites people to suggest ways to make it easily accessible. President Obama may not be too concerned about losing social media presence as he leaves office, given his own Twitter handle has around 78.5 million followers. It will be interesting to see how the next president uses technology to engage with the public in the years to come. Hopefully, they won't rely on private email servers. For more information on the White House's archival process, follow @WHWeb on Twitter.

This post was written with an older stylesheet. While LightDM or GDM may seem like a minor issue, it's not the only problem. The File Manager, File Previewer (also known as Sushi), and Scroll bars are all affected. Installing GS (Gnome Shell) in Ubuntu will give you a significantly different experience than running Vanilla Gnome. This isn't a comprehensive review, as many aspects are missing and still not ready for testing. For example, Pin Unlocking is not available (or I may have compiled it incorrectly), and I couldn't test notifications under Shield due to it crashing. GDM Login Screen: Choose User, Login, Sign in as a different user, and Time out. If you leave an input screen open for too long, GS will revert to the previous step. Gnome Shell Lock Screen: This new lock screen features a Curtain effect and a missing Pin un-locker. GDM and Lock screens appear similar but are separate modules with the same design. They are both theme-able, which may alleviate some concerns. The blue-curtain design with a large white time may not appeal to everyone. Ubuntu: Unfortunately, as long as there isn't a great Distro like Ubuntu, Gnome will be tightly linked to it. Most users run Gnome Shell through Canonical's product, which worked well for many years. However, it now feels like the relationship between Ubuntu and Gnome is broken. The issues are complex, involving incompatibilities between Compiz/Clutter, LightDM and GDM, and discussions about removing Nautilus or un-maintained systemD. The bottom line is that you can't achieve a Vanilla Gnome experience in Ubuntu, regardless of who's at fault.
Walter Breuning, who passed away at 114, lived a life that encapsulates the rise of modern America. Born in 1896, Breuning's story spans nearly a century, and his experiences reflect the country's growth and transformation. A Montana native, he was only 26 days younger than Besse Cooper of Georgia, who holds the record for the oldest living person. Breuning's earliest memories date back to the early 20th century, when his father shared with him the stories of fighting in the Civil War. At 16, Breuning started working for the railroad, and by 20, he had enlisted to fight in World War I, although he never received a call to service. In 1919, the same year women gained the right to vote, Breuning bought his first car, only to complain that it scared horses away due to its noise. The Great Depression hit, and though he felt fortunate to keep his job, Breuning credited President Franklin D. Roosevelt's signing of Social Security as the nation's greatest achievement. By the time the US joined World War II, Breuning was deemed too old to fight, and by the time the Beatles released their first album, he had retired from the rail industry. Breuning, a longtime clerk, views the advent of computers as a positive change for the railroad industry, even as many of his friends lost their jobs due to automation.

Michigan is paying its top three football assistants $1 million each per year, making it the first public institution to do so. The university has committed to retaining defensive coordinator Don Brown and offensive coordinator Tim Drevno with contracts worth more than $10 million combined over the next five years. In addition to Brown and Drevno, passing coordinator Pep Hamilton has been lured away from the Cleveland Browns with a four-year deal worth $4.25 million. The terms of these contracts were obtained by The Associated Press via a Freedom of Information Act request. Brown's contract includes a $1 million annual salary for the first four years, plus a retention bonus of $300,000 on April 1 of this year and next year, and another $400,000 in April 2019 and 2020. Drevno's deal is worth $1 million per year, plus a $150,000 signing bonus. Athletic director Warde Manuel extended the offers to Brown and Drevno in December, before the Wolverines lost to Florida State in the Orange Bowl. Hamilton was offered the position in writing on January 9th, after the departure of Jedd Fisch to UCLA. Hamilton's salary will increase to $1.25 million in 2020. He also receives a $150,000 signing bonus and is eligible for retention bonuses of $450,000 in April 2018 and $250,000 the following year. Brown and Drevno have been part of Harbaugh's staff since his arrival at Michigan. Hamilton, who was an associate head coach for the Browns last season, joins the Wolverines after Fisch left for UCLA. Michigan announced that it will conduct three of its spring practices in Rome, just days after the NCAA banned schools from combining spring break and football practices, similar to what Harbaugh did last year in Florida.

In 1975, David Bowie was gifted a Kirlian photography machine by Thelma Ross of UCLA's parapsychology lab. The machine generates a high-voltage field to a photographic plate, resulting in a glowing corona discharge image of whatever is positioned on it. However, the color, shape, and intensity of the image are influenced by various factors, including humidity, grounding, and the amount of oil and sweat on the skin. As a person interested in the occult and the unusual, Bowie was intrigued by the possibility of capturing his own "aura." Bowie's interest in Kirlian photography became apparent through his experiments with the technique, which were showcased in the programme for his 1976 tour supporting Station to Station. He also used it to investigate what was happening to his body when he took drugs, comparing two Kirlian photographs of his fingertip, one taken before and another after consuming cocaine, beside a crucifix given to him by his father. The image of his fingertip fascinated him, and he featured it in the booklet for Earthling and used it as the cover art for the "Little Wonder" single.
On March 31, Detroit Tigers reliever Daniel Stumpf has cleared waivers, according to Anthony Fenech of the Detroit Free Press, who reported the news on Twitter. The team had announced that Stumpf had been offered a chance to return to Kansas City, although he also has the option to opt for free agency. On March 30, the Tigers placed Stumpf on waivers, which he personally informed reporters such as Evan Woodberry of MLive.com via Twitter. This move comes after Stumpf was taken in the Rule 5 draft by the Royals last winter. What's unique about this situation is that Stumpf was previously taken in the Rule 5 draft and returned to Kansas City last summer, only to be sent back to the Phillies. If Stumpf clears waivers, he would have the right to reject an assignment with the Royals and instead pursue free agency. Stumpf, now 26, only appeared in a few MLB games last season due to a PED suspension. During his time with the Royals' Double-A affiliate, he had a strong performance, boasting a 2.11 ERA and 11.0 strikeouts per nine innings while allowing just 1.7 walks per nine. However, he failed to build on that momentum in spring training, allowing four earned runs on five hits and five walks while striking out eight batters in 8 2/3 innings.

Many people who use laptops and smartphones daily probably charge their phones with the laptop. To simplify this process and reduce clutter, Intel is testing inductive charging. Simply place your phone next to the laptop, and it will start charging. According to The Verge, Intel's new all-in-one PC concept features inductive charging for the keyboard, but the company plans to expand this technology to include ultrabooks that can charge phones. Using an Acer Aspire laptop, the wireless charger is slim and doesn't significantly bulk up the ultrabook. When a compatible phone is in close proximity, the charger will beep and display a notification on the laptop screen. This technology aims to minimize the need for separate phone chargers, but it raises questions about whether it might make laptops' built-in power sources more necessary. While it's touted as a greener solution by eliminating extra cords, we'd like to know more about the efficiency and environmental impact of the transmitter and receiver components. We're concerned that the embodied energy of the transmitter might be higher than that of a standard USB cord. Moreover, we wonder if this technology will replace traditional cords entirely. A commenter on The Verge noted that while inductive charging is convenient for charging phones, people often plug their phones into laptops for storage purposes. Could inductive charging be a more sustainable way to charge phones? While the concept is promising, we need more information to determine its full potential.

Noam Chomsky, an 88-year-old intellectual and self-described libertarian socialist, has sparked outrage after calling the Republican Party the most dangerous organization in human history due to its inaction on global warming. In an interview with BBC News, Chomsky made the statement, saying, "Look, when I said it, I said it was a very outrageous statement, but is it true?" He was responding to a BBC interviewer who had rated the Republican Party worse than North Korea's Kim Jong Un or the ISIS terrorist group. Chomsky then asked, "Is ISIS dedicated to destroying the prospects for organized human existence?" The interviewer pointed out that ISIS is engaged in a civil war and has toppled the governments of at least two countries, including Syria and Iraq. Additionally, the group has committed numerous atrocities, including beheadings and religious persecution. Experts estimate that ISIS militants have killed over 33,000 people. Chomsky, however, argues that the Republican Party is worse because ISIS is not actively working to accelerate global warming. "What does it mean to say not only we're not doing anything about climate change, but we're trying to accelerate the race to the precipice?" Chomsky asked. He also pointed out that it doesn't matter whether ISIS genuinely believes in its cause or not. Chomsky, a professor emeritus at the Massachusetts Institute of Technology, has a long history of criticizing American "imperialism." He opposed the Vietnam war in the 1960s and 70s and saw the collapse of the Soviet Union as a victory for socialism, not capitalism.

Progressive Conservative Leader Patrick Brown has claimed a seat in the Ontario legislature in a by-election just four months after taking over as party leader. Long-time Progressive Conservative MPP Garfield Dunlop stepped down from his Simcoe North seat this summer, paving the way for Brown to run. Brown won the party leadership in May and subsequently resigned his federal seat in the nearby Barrie riding. A significant shift in tone was observed in Dunlop's resignation, as he transitioned from being one of Brown's most vocal critics to a more conciliatory stance, ultimately endorsing Brown in Simcoe North. Brown effectively leveraged his canvassing and campaign skills, honed during the party leadership contest, where he defeated caucus favourite Christine Elliott. The early results showed Brown securing over 50% of the vote, outperforming Liberal candidate Fred Larsen and NDP candidate Elizabeth Van Houtte, who is a professor of social work at Lakehead University.

We previously explored the main factors that lead to job losses resulting from our EU membership under current terms. Today, I aim to provide a prudent estimate of the number of jobs lost due to our membership. The primary cause of job loss is in manufacturing, primarily due to the increased cost of energy. The shift towards cleaner energy sources has led to the closure of petrochemical plants, aluminium smelting facilities, steel production, and other energy-intensive industries. As a result, we no longer produce all our own power, instead relying on imports from France via the interconnector. If we had higher energy prices similar to those in the US, coupled with increased domestic production of oil, gas, and shale gas, as well as German-style coal-fired power stations, we could have gained around 450,000 extra jobs in manufacturing, or approximately 15% more jobs. Additionally, this would have led to an increase in energy-related jobs, potentially adding 50,000 extra positions, or around 10% more. Domestic policies could also have boosted agricultural and fishing jobs, with estimates suggesting an additional 30,000 or 10% more jobs. When considering the overall impact, the figure exceeds 500,000 extra jobs if the UK had more control over its own industries, energy production, and business regulations. Furthermore, services, the largest sector in our labour market, could have also benefited from these changes, potentially yielding further gains.
The 16th annual Opening Our Doors festival is back, and this year it promises to be bigger and better than ever. On Monday, October 9, the festival will feature over 80 free events, including special performances by the Huntington Theatre Company and guided gallery walks through some of Boston's finest art institutions. To keep you in the loop, the festival team will be sending out a weekly Weekender newsletter with the latest updates on the coolest things to do around Boston. The festival is a collaboration between more than 20 community organizations, youth performers, and artists, all working together to bring cultural activities to the residents of Boston. Kelly Brilliant, executive director of the Fenway Alliance and founder of Opening Our Doors, believes that the festival provides an opportunity for everyone to experience the cultural riches of the Fenway Cultural District without any financial burden. This year's festival will feature a wide range of activities, including art gallery walks through the Gardner Museum and the Museum of Fine Arts, tours of the Back Bay Fens, and performances by the Boston Children's Chorus and the Sociedad Latina Youth Alumni Band. The festival also includes acts geared towards young adults and college students, with performances by the Harry Potter Soundtrack Orchestra and Berklee's all-male a cappella group, the CharlieChords, at Northeastern's Krentzman Quad. One of the highlights of the festival is the American Therapy Booth, an interactive art installation by Julie Ann Otis, where attendees can share their thoughts and feelings about America while watching their responses being drawn into art. Brilliant praises Otis' approach, saying it's nonjudgmental and nonthreatening, and doesn't take any political sides. The festival also offers a range of events for theater lovers, including an open house by the Huntington Theatre Company, where attendees can see performances from Merrily We Roll Along and meet the theater's managing director, Michael Maso. Despite the gloomy weather forecast, the Fenway Alliance is committed to keeping all activities running, with many moving indoors when necessary. Brilliant notes that the festival is a unique opportunity for the community to come together without any financial cost. She says, "I think in an ever-divisive world, to have one day that's for everyone and cost is not a barrier... I think it's special."

Brian Armstrong, CEO and Co-founder of Coinbase, is pleased to announce that David Marcus, Head of Messenger at Facebook, will be joining Coinbase's Board of Directors. David brings firsthand experience of developing impactful, mobile-first products at scale, which will enrich the Coinbase board and support the leadership team as the company strives to become the most popular and safest platform for buying and selling digital currencies. Prior to his role at Facebook, David was President of PayPal, where he oversaw the company's global expansion and product strategy. During his tenure, PayPal regained its focus on technology and product innovation, won back developers and small businesses, and acquired Braintree, the parent company of Venmo, further accelerating the company's growth. David joined PayPal after the acquisition of his previous startup, Zong, and led mobile products before assuming the leadership role. David's expertise in product development and his knowledge of both the payments and mobile sectors will be invaluable to Coinbase as it pursues its mission of creating an open financial system that brings opportunities to people worldwide. As a long-time admirer of cryptocurrencies, David is excited to collaborate with Coinbase and its leadership team to make this vision a reality. David Marcus has been fascinated by cryptocurrencies since 2012 and has witnessed Coinbase's efforts to democratize access to this new asset class. He believes that the company's work has the potential to significantly improve people's lives and looks forward to contributing to this endeavor.

The Canadian Army has welcomed its first Textron TAPV (Tactical Armoured Patrol Vehicle) at Gagetown, New Brunswick. The six vehicles will be used to train operators and maintainers. Over the next 17 months, the fleet of 500 TAPVs will be distributed across seven bases and 24 units. The Canadian Army aims to declare full operational capability by mid-2020, following the training of all operators, as well as the completion of user trials and exercises to confirm operational readiness. The TAPVs from Textron are being delivered in two variants, General Utility and Reconnaissance. Equipped with remote weapons stations, gunners can aim and fire from the interior of the vehicle. These stations are equipped with both a 40-mm automatic grenade launcher and a C6 machine gun, according to the army.

A Philadelphia firefighter is facing backlash after a photo he posted online sparked controversy. The image, which shows him wearing a Confederate flag hat, holding a burning tiki torch, and has a caption referencing a trip to Virginia, has been deemed insensitive and racist by some. The firefighter, John Deluisi, has apologized for the post, saying he was drunk when he took the photo and tagged an African American co-worker at the Philadelphia Fire Department. Deluisi claims the photo was meant as a bad joke, a response to a previous post referencing the Charlottesville violence that erupted in the city just days prior. He admitted it went too far and has since been taken down, but not before offending many residents who pay his salary. The city's mayor, Jim Kenney, has called the post "deeply disturbing," and the fire department has launched an investigation that could result in disciplinary action. For Deluisi, the incident could have serious consequences, including potentially ending his nearly 20 years as a career firefighter.
In a dramatic stoppage-time equaliser, Liam Sercombe salvaged a point for Exeter City against Portsmouth. The hosts took the lead on the nine-minute mark when Jake Jervis scored from just six yards after a Ben Chorley knock-down. However, Ryan Taylor had a chance to seal the game when a loose back pass from the Exeter goalkeeper, Artur Krysiak, was missed, but his shot somehow ended up in the side-netting. As the clock ticked down, Sercombe's shot deflected off a Portsmouth player, leaving the keeper, Trevor Carson, stranded. The result sees Exeter City move six points above the relegation zone, while Portsmouth now find themselves four points ahead. Post-match, Portsmouth manager Richie Barker praised his team's attitude, saying, "I couldn't fault the players, their attitude was fantastic." He also questioned the accuracy of the throw-in that led to the goal, adding, "I thought that was our throw-in." Barker expressed frustration over the perceived extra four minutes of injury time, stating, "I'm not sure where those four minutes came from." The draw marked Pompey's fifth away game without a defeat, a testament to their growing resilience on the road. Barker acknowledged the positives, but was disappointed by the result, saying, "It's tough to take." Despite a recent slump, Barker reassured that his team is moving in the right direction, pointing out that they had previously lost five consecutive games six and eight weeks prior.
The suspect in the murder of an RTI activist in Mangalore is a former leader of the NaMo Brigade, a youth group that supported Prime Minister Narendra Modi before the 2014 Lok Sabha elections. According to an Indian Express report, police have launched a search for Naresh Shenoy, one of the brigade's founders and a close associate of the RSS in Karnataka. The investigation has revealed his and three other associates' involvement in the murder of 51-year-old Vinayak Pandurang Baliga, who was hacked to death by unknown people on March 21. Baliga was on his way to the temple when he was brutally attacked with a sharp-edged weapon. Mangalore Police Commissioner M Chandrashekhar stated that Baliga was attacked outside his house at 5:30 AM and died on his way to the hospital. A search was conducted at Shenoy's residence in Mangalore as part of the murder probe. Shenoy has been missing for over a week, and his cell phone has been switched off. Mangalore police had arrested two people, Nishith Devadiga and Vinith Poojary, soon after the arrest. Further investigations confirmed their role in the murder, allegedly contracted through a chain of operators, including close associates employed by Shenoy. Two persons arrested so far were allegedly contracted for a small sum by a person identified as Shivu, who was in contact with Shenoy's associate Shrikanth. The police issued public notices declaring Shivu and Shrikanth as prime suspects in Baliga's murder. Shrikanth, a former activist of a Hindutva group in Mangalore, was employed by Shenoy to manage operations of a few hostels in the city. Investigations also found that another worker employed by Shenoy, identified as Vignesh, was at the scene of the crime with a getaway car, a Qualis, to help the contract killers flee the spot. Police sources said a search is on to find Vignesh and the car. Baliga, a BJP worker, was involved in a battle with authorities at the local Venkataramana Temple over alleged misappropriation of temple funds to the tune of Rs 9 crore, which he discovered by investigating and filing RTI applications. He had filed as many as 92 RTI applications over various issues, including land encroachment and illegal buildings in Mangalore. Police believe he was primarily targeted over the row surrounding Venkataramana Temple, which belongs to the Saraswat Goud Brahmin
Mitt Romney strongly condemned Donald Trump's presidential bid in an interview with CNN's Wolf Blitzer on June 10, 2016. Trump's statements, Romney claimed, would irreparably harm the character of future generations of Americans. "I don't want to see a president who says things that change the very nature of our nation," Romney said, highlighting the dangers of trickle-down racism, bigotry, and misogyny. Romney even considered voting for Libertarian candidate Gary Johnson if Bill Weld were his running mate, saying he would evaluate Johnson's candidacy over the coming weeks and months. However, Romney ruled out running for president himself or voting for Hillary Clinton, the likely Democratic nominee. When asked if he was shirking his responsibility by not endorsing Clinton, Romney argued that his duty was to express his opinions to the American people, which he did in his criticism of Trump.

Lee Kleinman, a council member, initially supported a fee-based ordinance to reduce litter, but later changed his mind, claiming he should focus solely on his own district, North Dallas. He stated that he shouldn't care about the conditions in other areas of the city, including those with trash problems, unless they directly impacted his district. Kleinman's views sparked concern among some of his colleagues. In contrast, Vonciel Jones Hill, who has opposed any ban or bag tax, was absent from the vote. Monica Alonzo also voted against the ordinance, but remained silent. The American Progressive Bag Alliance criticized the vote, stating it would harm consumers and fail to achieve environmental goals, while jeopardizing 4,500 Texas jobs. The alliance's executive director, Lee Califf, described the vote as an example of "environmental myths and junk science driving poor policy in the plastic bag debate." However, it remains unclear whether the state will allow Dallas' new bag "ban" or bag tax. Attorney General Greg Abbott will examine the legality of the ordinance, following a request by state Rep. Dan Flynn on behalf of the Texas Retailers Association. Jerry Allen questioned Dallas City Attorney Warren Ernst about the state's stance on bag bans. Ernst stated that the city would defend the ordinance if it passed, but acknowledged uncertainty surrounding the issue. Council members opposed to the ordinance argued that Dallas needs to improve its enforcement of litter laws, citing the $4 million spent annually on trash pick-up without adequate results. Council member Scott Griggs noted that the issue is just one step in a larger effort to address trash and other environmental concerns.
A 23-year-old man from Papakura, Jared Kelly, has been banned from owning animals for five years and fined over $850 after pleading guilty to neglecting his dog. In June last year, an SPCA inspector discovered Kelly's dog, a boxer/staffordshire terrier cross, chained up with no shelter. The dog was so severely malnourished that its bones were visible, and it had lost all strength to bark. It also had severe flea and worm infestations, overgrown claws, and open sores on its front legs and rump. Kelly claimed he had simply lost interest in the dog and considered putting it down, but he eventually surrendered it to SPCA Auckland. The SPCA's executive director, Bob Kerridge, described the case as "heartbreaking" where an animal dependent on its owner for attention and affection was left chained up with no food or shelter due to the owner's loss of interest. Kerridge stressed that neglecting an animal to the point of starvation was unacceptable. Unfortunately, the dog was later euthanized due to behavioral problems that made it impossible to rehome responsibly, which Kerridge attributed to the dog's prolonged neglect.
A CCTV image from Brussels Airport surveillance cameras, made available by the Belgian Police, appears to show suspects in the Brussels airport attack on March 22, 2016. The image was captured by Reuters. Two brothers, Khalid El Bakraoui and Brahim El Bakraoui, are believed by officials to be the perpetrators of the Brussels airport attack. According to two sources familiar with the matter, the brothers were on the US government's counterterrorism watch lists before the March 18 arrest of Salah Abdeslam, a French national accused of a key role in the November 13 Paris attacks. Belgian prosecutors have identified Brahim El Bakraoui as one of the suicide bombers who attacked Brussels' Zaventem Airport, while they say Khalid El Bakraoui was responsible for the suicide bombing at Brussels' Maelbeek Metro station, near the European Union headquarters.
Elizabeth Warren steps onto the stage, having emerged victorious over incumbent Senator Scott Brown on November 6, 2012. This could have been a different outcome if Wall Street had simply allowed her to take the job she originally sought. The news is announced by The Huffington Post: nearly two years after the financial industry lobbied tirelessly to prevent consumer advocate Elizabeth Warren from leading the Consumer Financial Protection Bureau, she will now join the Banking Committee, according to four sources. This is a significant victory for progressives who fought hard to secure her a seat on the committee, which oversees the implementation of key banking regulations, including the Dodd-Frank Act. Warren played a crucial role in setting up the consumer protection bureau, but ultimately faced opposition from banking lobbyists and their Republican allies in the Senate, blocking her from leading the agency. In response, she ran for Senate in Massachusetts, ending the moderate tenure of Senator Scott Brown. Now, Warren will have a front-row seat on the panel that has the power to summon Wall Street bankers and other executives to testify before Congress.
Are you thinking of making a career change? Maybe to the automotive industry? Well, you're in luck because Tesla Motors in Australia is on the hunt for a lot of new staff as it rapidly expands its operations in the country. The company has announced a significant recruitment drive, with over 25 jobs available across Sydney and Melbourne. These roles range from retail sales and technical expert positions to behind-the-scenes positions for tech enthusiasts. The reason for this surge in hiring is the immense popularity of Tesla's Victorian operation in the Chadstone shopping centre, as well as the upcoming opening of a new Melbourne showroom, gallery, and service centre with Superchargers in the Richmond suburb. Additionally, the demand for Tesla's new base model all-wheel-drive Model S 70D is also a factor. The Sydney store in Artarmon is growing its staff, too, and one of the new hires will be a charging specialist who can guide customers through the process of installing a Tesla charger at home or using the national Supercharger network. Tesla has planned to cover the entire Australian east coast with Superchargers, making long-distance trips more feasible. The company is also looking for a couple of technicians who can work on both electric and non-electric vehicles, as well as two detailers, one for Melbourne and one for Sydney, to ensure your new Tesla looks sleek and well-maintained during regular service inspections and check-ups. If you're a tech-savvy individual, this could be a great opportunity to join a rapidly expanding company that's poised for success.
Russian President Vladimir Putin has announced that Russia will help India build at least 10 new nuclear reactors, following a recent visit to the country. The two nations have signed several major agreements on energy and defense. Russia will continue to be India's top defense supplier, with a new joint venture to support hydro-electric power projects also set to begin. The deal includes a commitment to manufacture nuclear components in India. Additionally, a $1 billion joint venture to supply India with 10 million tonnes of oil per year has been agreed. This follows a broader effort by Russia to expand its ties with Asia, amid Western sanctions. India is facing energy shortages, while Russia seeks to capitalize on this by increasing its exports to the region. The country is also looking to boost its diamond trade with Russia, which is the world's largest producer of rough diamonds. Russia will help India build the new reactors over the next 20 years, with a focus on manufacturing nuclear components locally. Mr. Putin's visit comes as tensions between Russia and the West continue, with the US, EU, and other countries imposing sanctions on Russia.
The Punjab and Haryana High Court has issued a notice to the SSP of Kapurthala district, asking him to explain why contempt proceedings shouldn't be initiated against him for failing to act on a complaint about self-styled 'godwoman' Sukhwinder Kaur alias Radhe Maa. The single bench of Justice Daya Chaudhary passed the directions after a resident of Phagwara, Surinder Mittal, filed a complaint alleging that Radhe Maa had hurt religious sentiments, threatened others, and committed other IPC offences. Mittal had initially approached the police, but when no action was taken, she sought directions from the high court. In 2015, Mittal had filed a complaint against Radhe Maa, and the then single bench of the high court had directed the SSP to investigate the allegations, determine if any cognizable offence was made out, and then take action. However, the SSP took no action, despite being reminded about the court order. As a result, Mittal approached the high court again and filed a contempt petition.

Los Angeles has been actively searching for a top-notch defenseman, and it appears they've finally found the right player. Notably, they've managed to secure him without having to part with Justin Williams due to salary constraints. In fact, as of now, Williams is likely to stay, as the market for a long-term defenseman wasn't substantial enough for General Manager Dean Lombardi to make a significant trade. It's a move that may seem unusual at first, but Kings fans will likely grow to appreciate it over time. The Kings are particularly drawn to McNabb's toughness, and his shot may be underrated. There's more to come on this story. China's leaders have imposed a five-year ban on the construction of government buildings, as part of a campaign aimed at curbing corruption and reducing public spending. The move follows criticism of lavish government offices and buildings, which have long been a source of public disapproval. President Xi Jinping has spearheaded an effort to eliminate waste and excess among senior officials, a move that has alienated many ordinary citizens. According to the directive issued by the Communist Party's central committee and the State Council, all new construction of official buildings is halted, including those built as training centers, hotels, and government motels. The ban also applies to seaside resorts, where officials have been able to stay for free or at discounted rates. Liu Shanying, a politics researcher at the Chinese Academy of Social Sciences, notes that these types of buildings can be a form of corruption, as they often involve significant government spending on operating costs, food, and other expenses. "Some office buildings use up a lot of money, with operating costs and expenses for eating and drinking all coming from government funds," he said. "This is a kind of corruption." The five-year ban is seen as a significant step in the fight against corruption. The directive also orders officials to consolidate their offices, with those holding multiple posts limited to a single office. Additionally, the ruling calls on party and government bodies to be more frugal and ensure that government spending is directed towards economic development and public welfare. However, officials will still be allowed to spend money on restoring government offices, according to the Xinhua News Agency. In the past, there have been restrictions on constructing new government buildings, but some departments and localities have continued to build in violation of regulations.
